ECK120031172	ECK120011413	ECK120010767	ECK120016808	repressor	-39.0				MarA plays a very important role in the complex negative regulation of the <i>hdeAB-yhiD</i> operon during the stationary phase and acid resistance that depends on the growth conditions, on other regulators of <i>hdeAB-yhiD</i> expression, and on the degree of induction of <i>marA</i> expression. MarA also controls it, by modifying the effects of the other regulators. This transcriptional regulator binds to a  marbox  partially overlapping the -35 box of the hdeAp promoter, competing with the RNA polymerase for DNA binding and/or direct interactions between MarA and &sigma;<sup>70</sup>, &sigma;<sup>38</sup>, or other subunits of RNA polymerase. In addition, several putative binding sites are located near the  marbox . MarA reduces the repression caused by GadX and Lrp during exponential phase and it helps H-NS repression, although it is not clear how. On the other hand, MarA reduces the ability of GadE to activate the <i>hdeAB-yhiD</i> operon during the stationary phase, since they compete for DNA binding or for interacting. This regulator also reduces the repression caused by GadW during stationary phase. Finally, MarA seems to compete functionally with GadX, GadW, RpoS, and Lrp under some conditions, which might ensure that <i>hdeAB-yhiD</i> expression is not repressed more than necessary <a href="#myRef" class="linkBlue">Ruiz C,2008</a>. ECK120031680	ECK120012855	ECK120011018	ECK120012873	repressor	-58.5				When the CTP level within the cell is high relative to the level of GTP, the <i>pyrD</i> gene is transcribed from a start site that allows formation of a secondary structure within the 5' end of the mRNA. ECK120032394	ECK120029342	ECK120010257	ECK120013232	activator	-105.0				RcsB is apparently essential for <i>cps</i> expression. As a matter of fact, both RcsA and RcsB are required for optimal <i>cps</i> expression, since <i>cps</i> expression in an <i>rcsB</i> strain is low and <i>cps</i> expression cannot be activated by RcsA in the absence of RcsB, suggesting an auxiliary role in cps expression. But RcsA is not absolutely dependent on RcsB. There are no <i>in vitro</i> data that demonstrate RcsA binding to the <i>cps</i> promoter region. Thus, direct interaction of RcsB and/or RcsA in the <i>E. coli</i> <i>cps</i> promoter region remains to be shown. RcsA and RcsB are proposed to form heterodimers in order to be functional in the activation of <i>cps</i>. Multicopy RcsB can overcome the absence of RcsA to activate <i>cps</i> expression. Osmotic shock has been shown to be dependent on RcsA, RcsB, RcsC, and MdoH. Several global regulators bind and repress cps, such as CRP and H-NS.	ECK12	attgtcaaccTAAAGAAACTCCTAAaaaccatatt
